% Custom commands for story placement using TikZ for rounded corners
\newcommand{\storybox}[3]{% #1=x, #2=y, #3=text
  \begin{textblock}{3}(#1,#2)
    \noindent%
    \begin{tikzpicture}
      \node[rectangle, rounded corners=3pt, fill=white, inner sep=0.1in, text width=2.55in, align=left] {%
        \small\sffamily #3%
      };
    \end{tikzpicture}%
  \end{textblock}%
}

\vspace{0.5in}

{\large\sffamily A Procedurally Generated Novel}

\vfill

{\normalsize\sffamily Generated November 22, 2025}

% About page
\newpage
\section*{About This Novel}

\noindent\textit{No Time to Discourse} is a speculative atlas that explores climate disaster across North America through interactive mapping and generative flash fiction.

\vspace{0.3in}

This novel was generated for NaNoGenMo (National Novel Generation Month), transforming the web-based interactive experience into a print format. Each page combines watercolor maps from Stamen Design with procedurally-generated stories created through RiTa.js grammars.

\vspace{0.3in}

Each of the stories in this novel is a work of fiction, yet each also attempts to capture at a human level the realities of climate disaster.

\vspace{0.3in}

\textbf{Original Web Project:} \url{https://notime.now/}

\textbf{Code Repository:} \url{https://github.com/samplereality/no-time-to-discourse-novel}

\clearpage

\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
  {\Large\textit{"The day is hot, and the weather, and the wars, and the King,\\
  and the Dukes; it is no time to discourse."}}

  \vspace{0.3in}

  --- Henry V
\end{center}

\storybox{2.78}{3.14}{\textbf{Norway House, Manitoba}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Sunday, March 26, 2028}\\
 It stormed for days, the rain streaming down in a cascade of celestial fury. Meanwhile Ivory spins up her TikTok channel, ranting about EMF weapons. Five thousand views and counting.}

\storybox{4.00}{5.76}{\textbf{Berens River, Manitoba}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Saturday, August 1, 2026}\\
 The aquifers run empty, and the soil is dust. Weathered docks lie uncovered in the scorching sun. The towns are barely holding on. It's a desert, thinks Kenzie. It hasn't rained in months. Meaningless words tumble around in her head. \textit{Outback, identities. Yoke}.}

\storybox{4.03}{8.29}{\textbf{Gimli, Manitoba}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Tuesday, December 5, 2028}\\
 The streams are empty, and the land is parched. Tangles of trash broil uncovered in the  sun. It's like the surface of Mars, thinks Elizabeth. It hasn't rained in what feels like years. The livestock are dead. She looks up to the sky and wonders what's next.}

\storybox{4.43}{0.68}{\textbf{Allakaket, Alaska}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Thursday, November 22, 2108}\\
 The old man in the documentary coughs and carries on. He's standing in front of the barricades. ``Things started getting bad in Allakaket in 2083,'' he says. ``Yeah, things were bad before that. But under the surface, you know? You couldn't see, especially if you didn't wanna see. But 2083, that was the year.''}

\storybox{3.52}{3.52}{\textbf{Hughes, Alaska}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Friday, November 22, 2047}\\
 At the Hughes checkpoint, immigration officers check papers with obvious impatience. ``You got sponsors?'' they sneer. A crowd surrounds the refugees, demanding ``We were here first!''}

\storybox{4.11}{6.23}{\textbf{Tanana, Alaska}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Thursday, November 22, 2096}\\
 At the Tanana checkpoint, volunteer guards check papers with barely concealed disgust. ``Quota's full for this month,'' they growl. A crowd surrounds the refugees, demanding ``Send them back!''}

\storybox{4.43}{3.49}{\textbf{Freeport, Texas}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Monday, February 16, 2026}\\
 Hurricane Dylan intensified over the warm Atlantic waters, catching meteorologists off guard. Dylan hunkered down in her mobile home, clutching her phone as the hail the size of golf balls pounded the walls. Coast Guard helicopters plucked her from her roof at dawn. She would never go home again.}

\storybox{4.02}{6.47}{\textbf{Bay City, Texas}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Monday, September 25, 2028}\\
 The dinoflagellate explosion began offshore, feeding on agricultural runoff in the warming waters. Within days, lifeless dolphins began washing ashore, spoiled seafood rotting in the sun. Tristan saw cleanup crews in hazmat suits collecting dead dolphins. }

\storybox{3.83}{0.96}{\textbf{Texas City, Texas}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Monday, February 22, 2027}\\
 An algal bloom crept through the Gulf. The neurotoxin spread beyond the water-Bryleigh could smell the decay just from breathing the sea breeze. And her partner Alanna. Alanna saw cleanup crews in hazmat suits collecting dead dolphins. }

\storybox{1.76}{5.31}{\textbf{Joliet, Illinois}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Tuesday, May 1, 2029}\\
 Averie boils her water before drinking. The storm didn't even have a name, she thinks. Valerie saw the flash flooding wash away whole communities, buildings, entire neighborhoods. The Autobahn Country Club. The flooding in Joliet didn't even make the national news. }
